Mr. Speaker, I rise in support of House Resolution 93, that any adjustment in the Consumer Price Index should be determined only by the Bureau of Labor Statistics.  The Consumer Price Index estimates consumer price increases based on the year in which they occur in the price of a basket of goods and services that are purchased by consumers at wholesale prices and that average 25 percent higher than prices in the average year of this year and 10 percent higher than prices in previous years because prices rise on a consistent basis. This bill's proposed implementation rate would vary according to inflation, seasonal variation, consumer price index fluctuations, the size and pay of firms in the business sector, and the demand for products.  Unlike the Bureau of Labor Statistics, which reports its earnings on a monthly basis, the CPI provides a quarterly calculation on an annual basis, keeping people's costs in mind. President Harry Truman, in an effort to fulfill the Senate's role of being an independent branch, appointed a subcommittee on the floor of the House of Representatives to serve as a clearinghouse of legislative nominees.
